<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2007 Atlantic hurricane season</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">

<td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane" title="Atlantic hurricane">Atlantic hurricane seasons</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, <a href="/wiki/2006_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2006 Atlantic hurricane season">2006</a>, <b>2007</b>, <a href="/wiki/2008_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2008 Atlantic hurricane season">2008</a>, <a href="/wiki/2009_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2009 Atlantic hurricane season">2009</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>2007 Atlantic hurricane season</b> was an active <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Atlantic hurricane season">Atlantic hurricane season</a>, although most of the storms were weak and short-lived. Despite the high activity of weak storms during 2007, it was the first season to feature more than one Category 5 landfalling hurricane, a feat that would not be matched until <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">2017</a>. It produced 17 <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone" title="Tropical cyclone">tropical cyclones</a>, 15 tropical storms, six hurricanes, and two major hurricanes. It officially started on June 1 and ended on November 30, dates which conventionally delimit the period during which most tropical cyclones form in the Atlantic Ocean. The first tropical cyclone, <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_(2007)" title="Subtropical Storm Andrea (2007)">Subtropical Storm Andrea</a>, developed on May 9, while the last storm, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Olga_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Olga (2007)">Tropical Storm Olga</a>, dissipated on December 13. The most intense hurricane, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean" title="Hurricane Dean">Dean</a>, is tied for the eighth most intense Atlantic hurricane ever recorded as well as the third most intense Atlantic hurricane at landfall. The season was one of only six on record for the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic</a> with more than one Category 5 hurricane. It was the second on record in which an Atlantic hurricane, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix" title="Hurricane Felix">Felix</a>, and an eastern Pacific hurricane, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Henriette_(2007)" title="Hurricane Henriette (2007)">Henriette</a>, made landfall on the same day. September had a record-tying eight storms, although the strengths and durations of most of the storms were low. Aside from hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean" title="Hurricane Dean">Dean</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix" title="Hurricane Felix">Felix</a>, none of the storms in the season exceeded Category 1 intensity.</p>
<p>Pre-season forecasts by <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Colorado State University</a> called for 14 named storms and 7 hurricanes, of which three were expected to attain major hurricane status. The <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a> (NOAA) later issued its initial forecast, which predicted 13 to 17 named storms, 7 to 10 hurricanes and three to five major hurricanes. After several revisions in the projected number of storms, NOAA and CSU lowered their forecasts by the middle of the season.</p>
<p>Several storms made landfall or directly affected land. Hurricanes Dean and Felix made landfall at Category 5 intensity, causing severe damage in parts of Mexico and Central America, respectively. Both storm names, as well as <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Noel" title="Hurricane Noel">Noel</a>, the name of a hurricane that affected the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>, were retired from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tropical_cyclone_names" title="List of tropical cyclone names">naming list</a> of Atlantic hurricanes. The United States was affected by five cyclones, although the storms were generally weak; three tropical depressions and only two tropical storms, <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Barry_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Barry (2007)">Barry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Gabrielle_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Gabrielle (2007)">Gabrielle</a>, and one hurricane, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Humberto_(2007)" title="Hurricane Humberto (2007)">Humberto</a>, made landfall in the country. Elsewhere, three storms directly affected Canada, although none severely. The combined storms killed at least 423 people and caused about $3 billion (2007 USD, $3.47 billion 2017 USD) in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[nb 1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_forecasts">Seasonal forecasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Seasonal forecasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Noted hurricane experts <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Philip_J._Klotzbach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Philip J. Klotzbach (page does not exist)">Philip J. Klotzbach</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_M._Gray" title="William M. Gray">William M. Gray</a>, and their associates at <a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">Colorado State University</a> issue <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_seasonal_forecasting" title="Tropical cyclone seasonal forecasting">forecasts of hurricane activity</a> each year, separately from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">NOAA</a>. Klotzbach's team, formerly led by Gray, determined the average number of storms per season between 1950 and 2000 to be 9.6 tropical storms, 5.9 hurricanes, and 2.3 major hurricanes (storms exceeding Category 3 on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_Hurricane_Scale" title="Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale">Saffir-Simpson Hurricane Scale</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_Dec_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_Dec-2">[1]</a></sup> A normal season, as defined by NOAA, has 9 to 12 named storms, of which five to seven reach hurricane strength and one to three become major hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPCAHOBI_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPCAHOBI-3">[2]</a></sup></p>
<table cellpadding="3" cellspacing="0" class="toccolours" style="float:right; margin-left:1em; text-align:right; clear: right;">
<caption><b>Predictions of tropical activity in the 2007 season</b></caption>

<td><b>Source</b></td>
<td><b>Date</b></td>
<td><b><span style="font-size: 80%;">Named<br/>
storms</span></b></td>
<td><b><span style="font-size: 80%;">Hurricanes</span></b></td>
<td><b><span style="font-size: 80%;">Major<br/>
hurricanes</span></b></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td align="left"><a href="/wiki/Colorado_State_University" title="Colorado State University">CSU</a></td>
<td align="left"><i>Average <span style="font-size: 80%;">(1950–2000)</span></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_Dec_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_Dec-2">[1]</a></sup></td>
<td>9.6</td>
<td>5.9</td>
<td>2.3</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-season_forecasts">Pre-season forecasts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-season forecasts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On December 8, 2006, Klotzbach's team issued its first extended-range forecast for the 2007 season, predicting above-average activity (14 named storms, seven hurricanes, three of Category 3 or higher).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_Dec_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_Dec-2">[1]</a></sup> It listed a 64 percent chance of at least one major hurricane striking the U.S. mainland. This included a 40 percent chance of at least one major hurricane strike on the <a href="/wiki/East_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="East Coast of the United States">East Coast</a>, including the Florida peninsula, and a 40 percent chance of at least one such strike on the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Coast_of_the_United_States" title="Gulf Coast of the United States">Gulf Coast</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Florida_Panhandle" title="Florida Panhandle">Florida Panhandle</a> westward. The potential for major hurricane activity in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> was forecast to be above average, and the team predicted that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" title="El Niño-Southern Oscillation">El Niño</a>, associated with reduced hurricane activity in the Atlantic, would dissipate by the active portion of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_Dec_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_Dec-2">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 3 a new forecast was issued, calling for a very active hurricane season of 17 named storms, nine hurricanes and five intense hurricanes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klotzbach_April_newsrelease_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Klotzbach_April_newsrelease-4">[3]</a></sup> The increase in the forecast was attributed to the rapid dissipation of El Niño conditions. The team also forecast a neutral or weak-to-moderate <a href="/wiki/La_Ni%C3%B1a" title="La Niña">La Niña</a> and noted that <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a> were much higher than average.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_April_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_April-5">[4]</a></sup> The estimated potential for at least one major hurricane to affect the U.S. was increased to 74 percent; the East Coast potential increased to 50 percent, and from the Florida Panhandle westward to <a href="/wiki/Brownsville,_Texas" title="Brownsville, Texas">Brownsville, Texas</a>, the probability rose to 49 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_April_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_April-5">[4]</a></sup> However, the team's report noted that while they predicted an active season, it was not suggesting that 2007 would be "as active as the 2004 and 2005 seasons".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klotzbach_April_newsrelease_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Klotzbach_April_newsrelease-4">[3]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Midseason_outlooks">Midseason outlooks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Midseason outlooks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On June 19 the UK Met Office (<a href="/wiki/Met_Office" title="Met Office">UKMO</a>) issued a forecast of 10 tropical storms in the July to November period with a 70 percent chance that the number would be in the range of 7 to 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UKMO_June_forecast_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-UKMO_June_forecast-6">[5]</a></sup> On August 3, 2007, Klotzbach's team lowered its season estimate to 15 named storms, of which eight were to become hurricanes and four to become major hurricanes. Team members noted that conditions had become slightly less favorable for storms than earlier in the year. Sea surface temperature anomalies were cooler, and several <a href="/wiki/Saharan_Air_Layer" title="Saharan Air Layer">Saharan Air Layer</a> events had suppressed development of tropical cyclones. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Ni%C3%B1o-Southern_Oscillation" title="El Niño-Southern Oscillation">El Niño-Southern Oscillation</a> (ENSO) conditions were also noted to have been slightly cooler.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gray_Aug_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gray_Aug-7">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 9, 2007, NOAA revised its season estimate slightly downwards to 13 to 16 named storms of which seven to nine were to be hurricanes and three to five major hurricanes. However, the agency reaffirmed its prediction of an above-average season, citing warmer-than-normal <a href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperature" title="Sea surface temperature">sea surface temperatures</a> in parts of the Atlantic Ocean and <a href="/wiki/Caribbean_Sea" title="Caribbean Sea">Caribbean Sea</a> and the likelihood of La Niña conditions during the peak of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NOAA_August_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-NOAA_August-8">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_summary">Season summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Season summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2007 Atlantic hurricane season">Timeline of the 2007 Atlantic hurricane season</a></div>
<center>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_56aa8e9fa1bf8708ae7481cb13a87084" name="timeline_56aa8e9fa1bf8708ae7481cb13a87084">
<area alt="Tropical Storm Olga (2007)" coords="709,100,795,120" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Olga_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Olga (2007)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Noel (2007)" coords="585,87,671,107" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Noel_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Noel (2007)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Lorenzo (2007)" coords="476,48,578,68" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Lorenzo_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Lorenzo (2007)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Karen (2007)" coords="479,35,570,55" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Karen_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Karen (2007)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Depression Ten (2007)" coords="457,9,538,29" href="/wiki/Tropical_Depression_Ten_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Depression Ten (2007)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Humberto (2007)" coords="432,113,540,133" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Humberto_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Humberto (2007)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Gabrielle (2007)" coords="423,87,537,107" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Gabrielle_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Gabrielle (2007)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Felix (2007)" coords="404,74,496,94" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Felix (2007)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Erin (2007)" coords="345,61,431,81" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erin_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Erin (2007)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Dean (2007)" coords="364,48,450,68" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Dean (2007)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Chantal (2007)" coords="295,35,398,55" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Chantal_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Chantal (2007)"/>
<area alt="Tropical Storm Barry (2007)" coords="108,22,200,42" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Barry_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Tropical Storm Barry (2007)"/>
<area alt="Subtropical Storm Andrea (2007)" coords="40,9,137,29" href="/wiki/Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_(2007)" shape="rect" title="Subtropical Storm Andrea (2007)"/></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/56aa8e9fa1bf8708ae7481cb13a87084.png" usemap="#timeline_56aa8e9fa1bf8708ae7481cb13a87084"/></div>
</center>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>Overall, the season's activity was reflected with a cumulative <a href="/wiki/Accumulated_cyclone_energy" title="Accumulated cyclone energy">accumulated cyclone energy</a> (ACE) rating of 74, which is below the long-term average of 93.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[8]</a></sup> ACE is, broadly speaking, a measure of the power of the hurricane multiplied by the length of time it existed, so storms that last a long time, as well as particularly strong hurricanes, have high ACEs. ACE is only calculated for full advisories on tropical systems at or exceeding 34 <a href="/wiki/Knot_(unit)" title="Knot (unit)">knots</a> (39 mph, 63 km/h) or tropical storm strength. Although officially, <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_cyclone" title="Subtropical cyclone">subtropical cyclones</a>, such as Andrea or the initial portions of Gabrielle, Jerry, and Olga, are excluded from the total,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[9]</a></sup> the figure above includes periods when storms were in a subtropical phase.</p>
<p>Only two major hurricanes—storms of Category 3 intensity or higher—formed during the season, the least since the <a href="/wiki/1997_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1997 Atlantic hurricane season">1997 season</a>, although tied with the <a href="/wiki/2006_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2006 Atlantic hurricane season">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/2002_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2002 Atlantic hurricane season">2002</a> seasons. Named storms were active for 33.50 days during the season, the lowest number of active days since the <a href="/wiki/1994_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1994 Atlantic hurricane season">1994 season</a>. There were only 11.25 days with active hurricanes, the lowest value since the <a href="/wiki/2002_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2002 Atlantic hurricane season">2002 season</a>. Despite this, the number of days with major hurricanes was above the long-term average. Four named storms made landfall on the U.S. during the year, but damage from those storms totaled to only about $82 million (2007 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Dollar" title="United States Dollar">USD</a>); this was the least damage the U.S. saw from any Atlantic hurricane season since the <a href="/wiki/1990_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1990 Atlantic hurricane season">1990 season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007report_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-2007report-11">[10]</a></sup> The season was one of only six Atlantic hurricane seasons to produce two Category 5 equivalent hurricanes, the others being the <a href="/wiki/1932_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1932 Atlantic hurricane season">1932</a>, <a href="/wiki/1933_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1933 Atlantic hurricane season">1933</a>, <a href="/wiki/1961_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1961 Atlantic hurricane season">1961</a>, <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">2017</a> seasons. The two Category 5 hurricanes, Dean and Felix, both reached Category 5 strength on two separate occasions, and both made landfall at Category 5 intensity, making the 2007 season the first to feature two hurricanes doing each, both of which would not be repeated until 2017. When Hurricane Felix was upgraded to a Category 5 storm on September 2, it became the eighth to form in this basin since 2000. This gave the decade more hurricanes of such strength than any other on record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HURDAT_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-HURDAT-12">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Tropical Depression Fourteen was upgraded to Tropical Storm Melissa on September 29, it was the eighth named storm to form in the month of September. That tied a record for the most storms during September, which was first set in <a href="/wiki/2002_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2002 Atlantic hurricane season">2002</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sept07tws_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-sept07tws-13">[12]</a></sup> Hurricane Humberto was the first hurricane to make landfall in Texas since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Claudette_(2003)" title="Hurricane Claudette (2003)">Hurricane Claudette</a> in <a href="/wiki/2003_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2003 Atlantic hurricane season">2003</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007report_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-2007report-11">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subtropical_Storm_Andrea">Subtropical Storm Andrea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Subtropical Storm Andrea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Subtropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_(2007).JPG"><img alt="Subtropical Storm Andrea (2007).JPG" data-file-height="7200" data-file-width="5600" height="193" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_%282007%29.JPG/150px-Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_%282007%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_%282007%29.JPG/225px-Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_%282007%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_%282007%29.JPG/300px-Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_%282007%29.JPG 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andrea_2007_track.png"><img alt="Andrea 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Andrea_2007_track.png/150px-Andrea_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Andrea_2007_track.png/225px-Andrea_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Andrea_2007_track.png/300px-Andrea_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>May 9 – May 11</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>95 km/h (60 mph) <small>(1-min)</small>  1001 <a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_Storm_Andrea_(2007)" title="Subtropical Storm Andrea (2007)">Subtropical Storm Andrea (2007)</a></div>
<p>The first storm of the season, Subtropical Storm Andrea, originated from a large <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> that formed off the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mid-Atlantic_States" title="Mid-Atlantic States">mid-Atlantic</a> coast on May 6. It deepened steadily along a cold front that pushed through <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>. When the system lost most of its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baroclinic" title="Baroclinic">baroclinic</a> support, development ceased until its low moved into warmer waters near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a>. However, interaction between the low and a strong high-pressure system to the north generated hurricane-force winds in the system. Decreasing vertical wind shear allowed the storm to generate deeper convection much closer to the center.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-andreatcr_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-andreatcr-14">[13]</a></sup> By May 9 the previously <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical cyclone</a> had transformed into Subtropical Storm Andrea while located about 140 miles (225 km) southeast of <a href="/wiki/Savannah,_Georgia" title="Savannah, Georgia">Savannah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-01LAdvisory1_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-01LAdvisory1-15">[14]</a></sup> Andrea began its subtropical phase as it was weakening, and continued this deterioration as it moved southward into an environment with higher wind shear. By May 11, Andrea had lost all significant convection and degenerated into a remnant low. Though it produced intermittent bursts of convection, Andrea's chance of regeneration was extinguished when an advancing cold front pushed it northward and eventually absorbed the system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-andreatcr_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-andreatcr-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Andrea was short-lived, dissipating on May 11. It was the first pre-season storm to develop since <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ana_(2003)" title="Tropical Storm Ana (2003)">Tropical Storm Ana</a> in April 2003 and the first Atlantic named storm in May since <a href="/wiki/1981_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Arlene" title="1981 Atlantic hurricane season">Tropical Storm Arlene</a> in 1981. Six people drowned along the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southeast_U.S." title="Southeast U.S.">Southeast U.S.</a> Coast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-andreatcr_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-andreatcr-14">[13]</a></sup> However, because Andrea never made landfall, most of the resulting damage was associated with large waves, higher than normal tides, associated coastal flooding, and beach erosion caused by the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-andreatcr_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-andreatcr-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Barry">Tropical Storm Barry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Barry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barry_01_jun_2007_1905Z.jpg"><img alt="Barry 01 jun 2007 1905Z.jpg" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="2000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Barry_01_jun_2007_1905Z.jpg/150px-Barry_01_jun_2007_1905Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Barry_01_jun_2007_1905Z.jpg/225px-Barry_01_jun_2007_1905Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Barry_01_jun_2007_1905Z.jpg/300px-Barry_01_jun_2007_1905Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Barry_2007_track.png"><img alt="Barry 2007 track.png" data-file-height="897" data-file-width="1024" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Barry_2007_track.png/150px-Barry_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Barry_2007_track.png/225px-Barry_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Barry_2007_track.png/300px-Barry_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 1 – June 2</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>60 mph (95 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  997 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Barry_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Barry (2007)">Tropical Storm Barry (2007)</a></div>
<p>On June 1, Tropical Storm Barry developed on the first day of the hurricane season. It originated from a <a href="/wiki/Trough_(meteorology)" title="Trough (meteorology)">trough</a> of low pressure in the southeastern <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a> that previously formed in the northwestern Caribbean. It accelerated to the northeast before reaching a peak intensity of 997 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mbar" title="Mbar">mbar</a> and making landfall on <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barrytcr_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-barrytcr-16">[15]</a></sup> Barry dissipated on June 2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barrytcr_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-barrytcr-16">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barrydeaths_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-barrydeaths-17">[16]</a></sup> In Florida, the rainfall resulted in slick roads, which caused two traffic-related deaths, and a woman was killed after being injured by rough surf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-barrydeaths_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-barrydeaths-17">[16]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Chantal">Tropical Storm Chantal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Chantal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chantal_31_july_2007_1328Z.jpg"><img alt="Chantal 31 july 2007 1328Z.jpg" data-file-height="1540" data-file-width="1320" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Chantal_31_july_2007_1328Z.jpg/150px-Chantal_31_july_2007_1328Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Chantal_31_july_2007_1328Z.jpg/225px-Chantal_31_july_2007_1328Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Chantal_31_july_2007_1328Z.jpg/300px-Chantal_31_july_2007_1328Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chantal_2007_track.png"><img alt="Chantal 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Chantal_2007_track.png/150px-Chantal_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Chantal_2007_track.png/225px-Chantal_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Chantal_2007_track.png/300px-Chantal_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 31 – August 1</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>50 mph (85 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  994 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Chantal_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Chantal (2007)">Tropical Storm Chantal (2007)</a></div>
<p>An area of low pressure formed near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bahamas" title="Bahamas">Bahamas</a> on July 28 and gradually began to organize while moving north-northeast. On July 30 it was classified as Tropical Depression Three and was named <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Chantal_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Chantal (2007)">Tropical Storm Chantal</a> shortly thereafter while south of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>. The storm weakened on August 1 and made landfall on <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>; it later tracked into the North Atlantic as an extratropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chantaltcr_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-chantaltcr-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chantal moved over the <a href="/wiki/Avalon_Peninsula" title="Avalon Peninsula">Avalon Peninsula</a> of <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a> where flooding was observed,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-chantaltcr_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-chantaltcr-18">[17]</a></sup> where about 4 inches (100 mm) of rain caused the postponement of the annual <a href="/wiki/Royal_St._John%27s_Regatta" title="Royal St. John's Regatta">Royal St. John's Regatta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> Insured damage across the area totaled $5.8 million (2007 <a href="/wiki/Canadian_dollar" title="Canadian dollar">CAD</a>; $5.5 million 2007 USD, $6.35 million 2017 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Dean">Hurricane Dean</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Hurricane Dean">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dean_20_aug_2007_1841Z.jpg"><img alt="Dean 20 aug 2007 1841Z.jpg" data-file-height="1780" data-file-width="1780" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dean_20_aug_2007_1841Z.jpg/150px-Dean_20_aug_2007_1841Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dean_20_aug_2007_1841Z.jpg/225px-Dean_20_aug_2007_1841Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Dean_20_aug_2007_1841Z.jpg/300px-Dean_20_aug_2007_1841Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dean_2007_track.png"><img alt="Dean 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dean_2007_track.png/150px-Dean_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dean_2007_track.png/225px-Dean_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Dean_2007_track.png/300px-Dean_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 13 – August 23</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>175 mph (280 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  905 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Dean" title="Hurricane Dean">Hurricane Dean</a></div>
<p>On August 11, a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> moved off the west coast of Africa, and, encountering favorable conditions, quickly spawned Tropical Depression Four, roughly 520 miles (835 km) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West-southwest" title="West-southwest">west-southwest</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deantcr_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-deantcr-21">[20]</a></sup> The depression moved briskly westward, south of a deep layered ridge,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc3_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc3-22">[21]</a></sup> and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Dean on August 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deantcr_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-deantcr-21">[20]</a></sup> The storm continued to strengthen overnight as it gained organization,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc8_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc8-23">[22]</a></sup> and became the first hurricane of the season on August 16.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deantcr_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-deantcr-21">[20]</a></sup> On August 17 the <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a> of the hurricane passed into the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> between the islands of <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a> as a Category 2 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td4disc17_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-td4disc17-24">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the warm waters of the Caribbean, Dean rapidly strengthened into a Category 5 hurricane with 165 mph (266 km/h) sustained winds. This made it the strongest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/North_Atlantic_tropical_cyclone" title="North Atlantic tropical cyclone">Atlantic hurricane</a> since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a>—and it was tied for the seventh most intense Atlantic storm of all time. An <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> weakened Dean, which then passed just south of Jamaica as a Category 4 hurricane. Dean regained Category 5 status late on August 20 and at that strength it made landfall on the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> near <a href="/wiki/Costa_Maya" title="Costa Maya">Costa Maya</a> on August 21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deantcr_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-deantcr-21">[20]</a></sup> Hurricane Dean was the first storm to make landfall as a Category 5 hurricane in the Atlantic basin since <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Andrew" title="Hurricane Andrew">Hurricane Andrew</a> in 1992. A <a href="/wiki/Dropsonde" title="Dropsonde">dropsonde</a> in the eye of the storm estimated a central pressure of 905 mbar, tying Dean with hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Camille" title="Hurricane Camille">Camille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Mitch" title="Hurricane Mitch">Mitch</a> for the seventh most intense Atlantic hurricane ever recorded. Dean was the third most intense landfalling Atlantic storm in history (after the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_Day_Hurricane_of_1935" title="Labor Day Hurricane of 1935">Labor Day Hurricane of 1935</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Gilbert" title="Hurricane Gilbert">Hurricane Gilbert</a> of <a href="/wiki/1988_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="1988 Atlantic hurricane season">1988</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deantcr_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-deantcr-21">[20]</a></sup> Dean weakened over land, but re-intensified slightly in the Gulf of Mexico. It made its final landfall near <a href="/wiki/Tecolutla" title="Tecolutla">Tecolutla</a>, Veracruz on August 22, dissipating the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deantcr_21-5"><a href="#cite_note-deantcr-21">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Hispaniola" title="Hispaniola">Hispaniola</a>, Dean killed 15 people and destroyed hundreds of homes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-reliefweb_2007-08-19_02-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_2007-08-19_jam_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP_2007-08-19_jam-26">[25]</a></sup> Dean also left $616 million (2007 USD, $711 million 2017 USD) in damage on <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a> and $154 million (2007 USD, $178 million 2017 USD) on <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> In Mexico, Hurricane Dean made landfall on the <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">Yucatán Peninsula</a> on August 21 as a Category 5 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-France24_07-08-18_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-France24_07-08-18-28">[27]</a></sup> Throughout its track, Dean killed 44 people<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2007report_11-2"><a href="#cite_note-2007report-11">[10]</a></sup> and caused several billion dollars in damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-deantcr_21-6"><a href="#cite_note-deantcr-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gleaner_july_4_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gleaner_july_4-29">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mar830cnn_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-mar830cnn-30">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Erin">Tropical Storm Erin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Erin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erin_15_aug_2007_1940Z.jpg"><img alt="Erin 15 aug 2007 1940Z.jpg" data-file-height="7150" data-file-width="5470" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Erin_15_aug_2007_1940Z.jpg/150px-Erin_15_aug_2007_1940Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Erin_15_aug_2007_1940Z.jpg/225px-Erin_15_aug_2007_1940Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Erin_15_aug_2007_1940Z.jpg/300px-Erin_15_aug_2007_1940Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Erin_2007_track.png"><img alt="Erin 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Erin_2007_track.png/150px-Erin_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Erin_2007_track.png/225px-Erin_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Erin_2007_track.png/300px-Erin_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 15 – August 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>40 mph (65 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1003 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Erin_(2007)" title="Tropical Storm Erin (2007)">Tropical Storm Erin (2007)</a></div>
<p>Tropical Storm Erin formed on August 16 in the Gulf of Mexico from a persistent area of convection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DRrain_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-DRrain-33">[32]</a></sup> Based on reconnaissance data received from an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NOAA" title="NOAA">NOAA</a> plane investigating the depression, it was upgraded to Tropical Storm Erin on August 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-td05update01_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-td05update01-34">[33]</a></sup> It weakened to a tropical depression as it made landfall near <a href="/wiki/Lamar,_Texas" title="Lamar, Texas">Lamar, Texas</a>, on August 16,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pa7a_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-pa7a-35">[34]</a></sup> and the NHC issued its last advisory on the system shortly thereafter as it moved inland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pa8_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-pa8-36">[35]</a></sup> Early on August 19 after entering <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma">Oklahoma</a>, the remnants of Erin suddenly re-intensified to maximum sustained winds of 60 mph (95 km/h) a short distance west of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oklahoma_City,_Oklahoma" title="Oklahoma City, Oklahoma">Oklahoma City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DRrain_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-DRrain-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>The storm flooded more than 40 homes and businesses. Along its path into the central states, Erin killed 16 people—9 directly—and left about $25 million (2007 USD, $28.9 million 2017 USD) in total damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-erintcr_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-erintcr-37">[36]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Felix">Hurricane Felix</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Hurricane Felix">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Felix_from_ISS_03_sept_2007_1138Z.jpg"><img alt="Felix from ISS 03 sept 2007 1138Z.jpg" data-file-height="1890" data-file-width="2772" height="102" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Felix_from_ISS_03_sept_2007_1138Z.jpg/150px-Felix_from_ISS_03_sept_2007_1138Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Felix_from_ISS_03_sept_2007_1138Z.jpg/225px-Felix_from_ISS_03_sept_2007_1138Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Felix_from_ISS_03_sept_2007_1138Z.jpg/300px-Felix_from_ISS_03_sept_2007_1138Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Felix_2007_track.png"><img alt="Felix 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Felix_2007_track.png/150px-Felix_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Felix_2007_track.png/225px-Felix_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Felix_2007_track.png/300px-Felix_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 31 – September 5</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>175 mph (280 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  929 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix" title="Hurricane Felix">Hurricane Felix</a></div>
<p>An area of disturbed weather east of the <a href="/wiki/Windward_Islands" title="Windward Islands">Windward Islands</a> was designated Tropical Depression Six on August 31. Early on September 1, it was named <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Felix" title="Hurricane Felix">Tropical Storm Felix</a>, and it was upgraded to a hurricane later that day. Tracking generally westward, it rapidly intensified to Category 5, and after fluctuating in strength, made landfall on <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> with 160 mph (260 km/h) winds. At least 133 deaths and more than $50 million (2007 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_Dollar" title="United States Dollar">USD</a>) in damage have been attributed to Felix.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-felix_damage_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-felix_damage-38">[37]</a></sup> With Felix, the 2007 Atlantic hurricane season became the first known to include two hurricanes making landfall at Category 5;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Felix_TCR_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-Felix_TCR-39">[38]</a></sup> hurricanes <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Irma" title="Hurricane Irma">Irma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Maria" title="Hurricane Maria">Maria</a> made landfall at Category 5 intensity during the <a href="/wiki/2017_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2017 Atlantic hurricane season">2017 Atlantic season</a>.</p>
<p>Hurricane Felix took a similar path as Hurricane Dean though a bit further south, although its effects were not severe; damage on <a href="/wiki/Tobago" title="Tobago">Tobago</a> was estimated at $250,000 (2007 <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago_dollar" title="Trinidad and Tobago dollar">TTD</a>; $40,000 2007 USD, $46.2 thousand 2017 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> Hurricane Felix made landfall just south of the border between <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>, in a region historically known as the <a href="/wiki/Mosquito_Coast" title="Mosquito Coast">Mosquito Coast</a>, as a Category 5 hurricane with 160 mph (260 km/h) winds on September 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Felix_TCR_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-Felix_TCR-39">[38]</a></sup> Residents of the region were reported to have been given little warning of the oncoming hurricane, which left many fisherman stranded at sea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> In all, Felix killed at least 130 people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Felix_TCR_39-2"><a href="#cite_note-Felix_TCR-39">[38]</a></sup> and damage in Nicaragua totaled C$869.3 million (2007 <a href="/wiki/Nicaraguan_c%C3%B3rdoba" title="Nicaraguan córdoba">NIO</a>; $46.7 million 2007 USD, $53.9 thousand 2017 USD).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-felix_damage_38-1"><a href="#cite_note-felix_damage-38">[37]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Gabrielle">Tropical Storm Gabrielle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2007_Atlantic_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Gabrielle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gabrielle_09_sept_2007_1800Z.jpg"><img alt="Gabrielle 09 sept 2007 1800Z.jpg" data-file-height="4000" data-file-width="3556" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gabrielle_09_sept_2007_1800Z.jpg/150px-Gabrielle_09_sept_2007_1800Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gabrielle_09_sept_2007_1800Z.jpg/225px-Gabrielle_09_sept_2007_1800Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Gabrielle_09_sept_2007_1800Z.jpg/300px-Gabrielle_09_sept_2007_1800Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gabrielle_2007_track.png"><img alt="Gabrielle 2007 track.png" data-file-height="633" data-file-width="1024" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Gabrielle_2007_track.png/150px-Gabrielle_2007_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Gabrielle_2007_track.png/225px-Gabrielle_2007_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Gabrielle_2007_track.png/300px-Gabrielle_2007_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
